9

Types of Dividends Paid by Corporations

1936 and 1937

The corporation income and excess-profits tax returns for 1936 and for 1937 included a special schedule for the detailed reporting of the types of dividends paid by corporations. Statistics compiled from these schedules provide, for the first time, information regarding (1) the relative importance of taxable and nontaxable dividend payments, (2) variations in the types of dividend payments by corporations of different income size classes, and (3) the composition of dividends paid in assets other than cash and the corporation's own stock.

The detailed information on types of dividends paid by corporations with net incomes subject to the surtax on undistributed profits for 1936 and 1937 is not complete because some corporations failed to supply the information requested in the special dividends schedule. Those supplying the requested information reported $6,798,568,000

Previously published figures showed that in 1936 a total of 92,660 corporations (including 7,062 with no net income) reported paying dividends. The comparable number for 1937 is 97,760 (including 9,674 with no net income). Dividends paid reported by all corporations for 1936 amounted to $7,724,304,000, of which $7,514,539,000 was paid by corporations with net income and $209,765,000 by corporations with deficits or no net income. For 1937 dividends paid reported by all corporations amounted to $7,702,687,000, of which $7,479,719,000 was paid by corporations with net income and $222,968,000 by corporations with deficits or no net income.

The date included in the present analysis relate not to all corporations but only to those corporations with net income subject to the surtax on undistributed profits which supplied detailed information on dividend payments (Schedule M for 1936, Schedule M for 1937) in their income tax returns. For 1936, 72,015 corporations reported taxable and 2,254 reported nontaxable dividend payments.

dividend payments for 1936 and $7,214, 490,000 for 1937. They accounted for 90.5 percent of all dividends paid by corporations reporting net income for 1936 and for 96.5 percent of all dividends paid by corporations reporting net income for 1937.

Almost all the dividends distributed by the corporations included in this analysis were reported as taxable, amounting to 96.5 percent for 1936 and 98.6 percent for 1937. Of the taxable dividends, by far the most important type distributed was "cash and assets other than the corporation's own stock." For 1936 and 1937, respectively, this item amounted to 95.7 percent and 97.8 percent of all dividend payments.

Based on the distribution of dividends as shown in Table 1, stock dividends were in general relatively unimportant. They amounted to 4.3 percent of the distributions for 1936 and 2.2

For 1937, 80,866 corporations reported taxable dividend payments in cash and assets other than the corporation's own stock; 756 reported taxable and 648 reported nontaxable dividend payments in the corporation's own stock. The total number of corporations included in this analysis is less than the aggregate of the number reporting the different types of dividend payments since in some instances the same corporation reported two or more types of dividends.

Corporations reporting deficits and corporations that were not subject to the surtax on undistributed profits (such as banks, insurance companies and other classes of corporations specified in section 14 of the Revenue Act of 1936) were not included in these tabulations.

The data on various types of taxable and nontaxable dividends represent the amounts and classification as reported by taxpayers, before audit by the Bureau of Internal Revenue.

11

percent of the distributions for 1937. The larger portion of these was reported as nontaxable. For 1936 and 1937 nontaxable stockdividends amounted respectively to 3.5 percent and 1.4 percent of distributions.

Information on types of dividend payments is available in more detail for 1936 than for 1937. The detailed data for 1936 presented in Table 2 show that cash alone accounted for 91.1 percent of dividend distributions and that all other types of dividends combined accounted for only 8.9 percent of the total. The 8.9 percent other than cash included 2.1 percent attributable to the obligations of the corporation (other than stock), 4.3 percent attributable to the corporation's stock of all kinds, and 2.5 per-

cent attributable to still other assets. Nontaxable stock dividends amounted to 3.5 percent of the dividend distributions and taxable stock dividends accounted for 0.8 percent. The nontaxable stock dividends for the most part were represented by common stock distributions, whereas the taxable stock dividends included a larger amount of preferred than common stock.

In general it appears that for corporations with small incomes the nontaxable dividends were relatively more important than for corporations with large incomes. This was also the case with most non-cash types of taxable dividends. In all of the income classes, at least five-sixths of the total dividends, however, were cash dividends.
